   <div class=\"partner-logo-alignment\">\n                <!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">Gravitational Lens System PS J0147+4630 (Andromeda's Parachute): Main Lensing Galaxy and Optical Variability of the Quasar Images</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Luis J. <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D0004-637X%2F887%2F2%2F126\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">0004-637X/887/2/126</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n             <P>Because follow\u2013up observations of quadruple gravitational lens systems are of extraordinary importance for astrophysics and cosmology, we present single-epoch optical spectra and <I>r</I>-band light curves of PS J0147+4630. This recently discovered system mainly consists of four images ABCD of a background quasar around a foreground galaxy G that acts as a gravitational lens. First, we use long-slit spectroscopic data in the Gemini Observatory Archive and a multi-component fitting to accurately resolve the spectra of A, D, and G. The spectral profile of G resembles that of an early-type galaxy at a redshift of 0.678\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001, which is about 20% higher than the previous estimate. Additionally, the stellar velocity dispersion is measured to ~5% precision. Second, our early <I>r</I>-band monitoring with the Liverpool Telescope leads to accurate light curves of the four quasar images. Adopting time delays predicted by the lens model, the new lens redshift, and a standard cosmology, we report the detection of microlensing variations in C and D as large as ~0.1 mag on timescales of a few hundred days. We also estimate an actual delay between A and B of a few days (B is leading), which demonstrates the big potential of optical monitoring campaigns of PS J0147+4630.</P> </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=0004-637X/887/2/126&doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ab5063&exportFormat=iopexport_bib&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-bib\" title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=0004-637X/887/2/126&doi=10.3847/1538-4357/ab5063&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2019ApJ...887..126G\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2019ApJ...887..126G\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/0004-637X/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjab5063s1\" name=\"apjab5063s1\">1.\u00a0Introduction</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Optical light curves of the four images of a quadruple gravitationally lensed quasar (quad) have a great potential to reveal physical properties of the lensed quasar, the main lensing galaxy, and the universe as a whole. Thus, monitoring campaigns of QSO 2237+0305 (Einstein Cross; Wo\u017aniak et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib35\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib35\">2000</a>; Alcalde et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib1\">2002</a>; Eigenbrod et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib9\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib9\">2008b</a>) have proved to be invaluable tools for unveiling the structure of the quasar accretion disk and the composition of the lensing galaxy (e.g., Shalyapin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib29\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib29\">2002</a>; Kochanek <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib17\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib17\">2004</a>; Eigenbrod et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib8\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib8\">2008a</a>). Most recently, light curves of other quads also led to important astrophysical results, e.g., an estimate of the accretion disk size in HE 0435\u22121223 and WFI 2033\u22124723 using microlensing-induced variations (Fian et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib11\">2018</a>; Morgan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib22\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib22\">2018</a>), and a robust measurement of the Hubble constant <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> from the time delays of HE 0435\u22121223, RXJ1131\u22121231, and B1608+656 (assuming a flat \u039bCDM cosmology with free energy density \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>; Bonvin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib4\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib4\">2017</a>). For a given quad, in addition to accurate time delays, the redshift and stellar velocity dispersion of the main lensing galaxy (and the properties of the lens environment) are required to obtain strong constraints on cosmological parameters (e.g., Suyu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib31\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib31\">2017</a>).</p><p>Berghea et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib2\">2017</a>) reported the serendipitous discovery of the bright quad PS J0147+4630 using multiband frames from the Panoramic Survey Telescope and Rapid Response System (Pan-STARRS; Chambers et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib7\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib7\">2016</a>). The four images of this first Pan-STARRS lensed quasar are not arranged like a cross, but rather resembling the shape of an open parachute (Andromeda's Parachute). An arc-like structure contains the three brightest images (A, B, and C; <em>r</em>\u00a0~\u00a016\u221216.5 mag), while the fourth component D (<em>r</em>\u00a0~\u00a018 mag) is located about 3'' from such arc. The main lensing galaxy (G; <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn1.gif\" alt=\"$r\\,\\sim $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">r\\,\\sim</script></span></span> 20 mag) and D are only ~1'' apart. Additionally, spectroscopic observations indicated the broad absorption line nature of the quasar, which has a redshift of 2.341\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001 (Lee <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib18\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib18\">2017</a>) and is absorbed by several intervening metal systems (Rubin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib24\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib24\">2018</a>). From long-slit optical spectroscopy with the Gemini Multi-Object Spectrograph (GMOS) on the 8.1 m Gemini North Telescope, Lee (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib19\">2018</a>) also found a lens redshift <em>z</em><sub>G</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.5716\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.0004. These redshifts and <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) imaging of the lens system allowed Shajib et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib27\">2019</a>) to predict time delays between the quasar images for a flat \u039bCDM cosmology with <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> and \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.7 (\u03a9<sub><em>m</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.3).</p><p>The Gravitational LENses and DArk MAtter (GLENDAMA) project is conducting optical observations of a sample of ten lensed quasars with bright images (<em>r</em> &lt; 20 mag) at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn2.gif\" alt=\"$1\\lt z\\lt 3$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1\\lt z\\lt 3</script></span></span> (Gil-Merino et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib12\">2018</a>). This representative sample includes the quad PS J0147+4630, which is being monitored with the 2.0 m Liverpool Telescope (LT) since 2017 August. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s2\">2</a>, we reanalyze the GNT\u2013GMOS data of PS J0147+4630 to accurately extract spectra for the three close sources within the slit (A, D, and G). We then focus on the new spectrum of G, measuring its redshift and the stellar velocity dispersion. Implications of this data reanalysis are also discussed in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s2\">2</a>. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s3\">3</a>, we present LT <em>r</em>-band light curves of the four images of PS J0147+4630 spanning two complete observing seasons from 2017 to 2019, and show the potential of optical monitoring programs of this quad. We summarize the paper in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s4\">4</a>.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjab5063s2\" name=\"apjab5063s2\">2.\u00a0Reanalysis of the GNT\u2013GMOS Spectroscopy: Main Lensing Galaxy</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Lee (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib19\">2018</a>) obtained GNT\u2013GMOS spectroscopic data of PS J0147+4630 on 2017 September 2, consisting of 4\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a01200 s long-slit exposures (B600 grating) taken under subarcsecond seeing conditions. The 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5-width slit with a spatial pixel scale of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1614 was oriented along the line joining A and D (and crossing G). We downloaded these publicly available observations<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjab5063fn1\">4</a></sup>\n to reanalyze them. Our aim was to accurately resolve the individual spectra of the three sources in the crowded region through a well-tested state-of-the-art technique (see below). Before doing the extraction of spectra for A, D, and G, usual data reductions were performed using the Gemini IRAF package.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjab5063fn2\">5</a></sup>\n Regarding the wavelength range and dispersion, they were 4403\u20137605 \u00c5 and 1.02 \u00c5 pix<sup>\u22121</sup>, respectively. We also inferred a resolving power of ~2500 from the 2.24 \u00c5 width of the 5577 \u00c5 [O <span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>] line in the night airglow.</p><p>We extracted the instrumental spectra of A, D, and G by fitting three 1D Moffat profiles in the spatial direction for each wavelength bin (e.g., Sluse et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib30\">2007</a>; Shalyapin &amp; Goicoechea <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib28\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib28\">2017</a>). For an extended source, a 1D point-spread function (PSF) model does not describe its total light. Therefore, because G was treated as a point-like object, we actually did not derive the overall spectrum of the galaxy. However, the flux ratio A/G is ~250, and the very faint galaxy does not play a relevant role when modeling the light distribution along the slit. This distribution is dominated by emission from A and D, so the critical issue is our ability to accurately account for the flux of both quasar images, minimizing the contamination of G. We used <em>HST</em> astrometry (Shajib et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib27\">2019</a>) to set the positions of D and G with respect to A. In regard to the 1D PSF model, we checked that a skewed Moffat profile (Sch\u00f6nebeck et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib26\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib26\">2014</a>) works better than the Gaussian or the symmetric Moffat one (see Appendix <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063app1\">A</a>; Moffat <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib21\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib21\">1969</a>). Thus, we adopted a skewed Moffat function with <em>a</em><sub>6</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0<em>a</em><sub>7</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00, i.e., only the asymmetry parameter <em>a</em><sub>5</sub> was considered (see Equation (10) of Sch\u00f6nebeck et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib26\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib26\">2014</a>). We also set the Moffat power-law index to an optimal value of 2. In a first fit to the multiwavelength 1D flux distribution, the position (centroid) of A, the width and asymmetry of the Moffat function, and the amplitudes of the three components were allowed to vary at each wavelength. We then fitted A positions and Moffat structure parameters to smooth polynomial functions of the observed wavelength, fixing position-structure parameters to their polynomial values and leaving only the three amplitudes as free parameters in a second iteration.</p><p>The four instrumental spectra of each source (one per exposure) were calibrated in flux and combined into a single spectral energy distribution. To carry out the flux calibrations, we used GNT\u2013GMOS\u2013B600 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5-width slit observations of the standard star EG 131 (Bessell <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib3\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib3\">1999</a>) on 2017 September 4. Final spectra of A, D, and G are included in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjab5063t1\">1</a> and plotted in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f1\">1</a>. A comprehensive analysis of the quasar spectra will be presented in a forthcoming paper. Here, we concentrate on the optical spectrum of the main lensing galaxy. The spectral slopes of G, as well as its Ca <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> <em>H</em>&amp;<em>K</em> doublet at about 6600 and 6660 \u00c5 and its <em>G</em>-band around 7225 \u00c5, are in very good agreement with an early-type galaxy template<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjab5063fn3\">6</a></sup>\n at <em>z</em> = 0.678 (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f1\">1</a>). After doing an initial estimate for <em>z</em><sub>G</sub> from the observed absorption features, we accurately measured the lens redshift using the Penalized PiXel-Fitting (pPXF) package<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjab5063fn4\">7</a></sup>\n (Cappellari &amp; Emsellem <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib6\">2004</a>; Cappellari <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib5\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib5\">2017</a>). This software compares the spectrum of G and stellar spectra, providing a correction to the initial value of <em>z</em><sub>G</sub> and measuring the stellar velocity dispersion. From the MILES Library of Stellar Spectra<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjab5063fn5\">8</a></sup>\n (S\u00e1nchez-Bl\u00e1zquez et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib25\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib25\">2006</a>; Falc\u00f3n-Barroso et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib10\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib10\">2011</a>), we obtained <em>z</em><sub>G</sub> = 0.678 \u00b1 0.001 and <em>\u03c3</em><sub>G</sub> = 313 \u00b1 14 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f2\">2</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjab5063f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjab5063f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0GNT\u2013GMOS\u2013B600 spectra of PS J0147+4630ADG in 2017 September. Flux is shown in a logarithmic scale to improve visibility, and gray highlighted bars are associated with gaps between the detectors. We note that the quasar spectra are reasonably well calibrated in flux, while the galaxy spectrum is not. The redshifted (<em>z</em> = 0.678) template of an early-type galaxy is also displayed for comparison purposes (see main text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjab5063f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadFigure/figure/apjab5063f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjab5063f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjab5063f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjab5063f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjab5063f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjab5063t1\">1</a> is published in its entirety in the machine-readable format. A portion is shown here for guidance regarding its form and content.</p>\n<a name=\"apjab5063t1fna\" id=\"apjab5063t1fna\"></a><sup> a</sup>Observed wavelength in \u00c5.\n<a name=\"apjab5063t1fnb\" id=\"apjab5063t1fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>Flux in 10<sup>\u221217</sup> erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup> s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u00c5<sup>\u22121</sup>.\n<a name=\"apjab5063t1fnc\" id=\"apjab5063t1fnc\"></a><sup> c</sup>Flux error in 10<sup>\u221217</sup> erg cm<sup>\u22122</sup> s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u00c5<sup>\u22121</sup>.\n\n\n\n<p>Only a portion of this table is shown here to demonstrate its form and content. A <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"webref\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/suppdata/apjab5063t1_mrt.txt\">machine-readable</a> version of the full table is available.</p>\n\n\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-table-data\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/suppdata/apjab5063t1_mrt.txt\" target=\"_blank\">Data</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/suppdata/apjab5063t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We note that our G spectrum and the redshifted template in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f1\">1</a> are very similar, while the G spectrum in Figure 2 of Lee (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib19\">2018</a>) does not resemble those of typical galaxies and seems to be heavily contaminated by quasar light. Thus, the previous identification of absorption lines of G is unreliable, and we adopt the new value of <em>z</em><sub>G</sub> as the lens redshift. For a flat \u039bCDM cosmology with <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> and \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0= 0.7, an 18.5% increase in the lens redshift, from 0.572 to 0.678, results in predicted time delays that are ~27% longer than those in Table C1 of Shajib et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib27\">2019</a>). These new delays are <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn3.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AB}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AB}}</script></span></span> = \u22122.7, \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AC</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22129, and \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AD</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0245 days (\u0394<em>t</em><sub>XY</sub> = <em>t</em><sub>Y</sub> \u2212 <em>t</em><sub>X</sub>). We also remark that the value of <em>z</em><sub>G</sub> plays a critical role in determining <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> from measured time delays of the system. If we assume that \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0+\u00a0\u03a9<sub><em>m</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a01 and <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn4.gif\" alt=\"$0.6\\leqslant {{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{\\Lambda }}}\\leqslant 0.8$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">0.6\\leqslant {{\\rm{\\Omega }}}_{{\\rm{\\Lambda }}}\\leqslant 0.8</script></span></span>, then 1.266\u00a0\u2264\u00a0<em>H</em><sub>0</sub>(<em>z</em><sub>G</sub> = 0.678)/<em>H</em><sub>0</sub>(<em>z</em><sub>G</sub> = 0.572)\u00a0\u2264\u00a01.270.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjab5063s3\" name=\"apjab5063s3\">3.\u00a0Optical Variability of the Quasar Images</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjab5063s3-1\" name=\"apjab5063s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0LT-IO:O Light Curves</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We monitored PS J0147+4630 with the LT from 2017 August to 2018 January and from 2018 July to 2019 February, i.e., during the first two visibility periods after its discovery. All observations were made using the Sloan <em>r</em>-band filter on the IO:O optical camera (pixel scale of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />30), and a single 120 s exposure was taken each observing night. Although we obtained 84 frames, six of them have poor quality and are not usable for doing photometry. Thus, in addition to basic instrumental reductions from the LT-IO:O pipeline, we used IRAF software<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjab5063fn6\">9</a></sup>\n (Tody <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib32\">1986</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib33\">1993</a>) to remove cosmic-rays and bad pixels from the remaining 78 frames. The central region of one of these usable frames is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f3\">3</a>. This includes the four quasar images, as well as an isolated and unsaturated star at R.A. (J2000)\u00a0=\u00a026<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />773246 and decl. (J2000)\u00a0=\u00a0+46<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />506670 (<em>r</em>\u00a0=\u00a016.606 mag) that allows us to build up an empirical 2D PSF. A bright field star at R.A. (J2000)\u00a0=\u00a026<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />746290 and decl. (J2000)\u00a0=\u00a0+46<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/fdg.gif\" alt=\"fdg\" align=\"baseline\" />504028 is also used as a control object having constant brightness <em>r</em>\u00a0=\u00a015.421 mag (see the middle right side of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f3\">3</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjab5063f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjab5063f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0LT-IO:O subframe of PS J0147+4630 in the Sloan <em>r</em> band. This subframe of size 3'\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a02' corresponds to the 120 s exposure in subarcsecond seeing on 2018 August 13. The field of view includes the quad with images ABCD (the strong lensing region is zoomed in on in the top sub-panel), the PSF star and the control star (see main text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjab5063f3\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadFigure/figure/apjab5063f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjab5063f3\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjab5063f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>For each of the 78 frames, the brightness of A, B, C, and D, and the control star were extracted through PSF fitting, using the IMFITFITS software (McLeod et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib20\">1998</a>) and the PSF star located in the center of the field of view in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f3\">3</a>. In the strong lensing region, ABCD and G were modeled as four point-like sources and a de Vaucouleurs profile convolved with the empirical 2D PSF, respectively. Our realistic overall model also incorporated several <em>HST</em> constraints: positions of B, C, D, and G with respect to A, and structure parameters of G (Shajib et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib27\">2019</a>). We applied the IMFITFITS code to the best frames to obtain the constant galaxy flux, and then to all frames (whatever their quality), fixing the galaxy flux and allowing the remaining parameters to vary, i.e., the absolute position of A and the four quasar fluxes (see Appendix <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063app2\">B</a>). In Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjab5063t2\">2</a>, we present values of the FWHM of the seeing disk and the signal-to-noise ratio (S/N) for the PSF star, along with the <em>r</em>-band magnitudes of the quasar images and the control star.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjab5063t2\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table its entirety in the machine-readable format. A portion is shown here for guidance regarding its form and content.</p>\n<a name=\"apjab5063t2fna\" id=\"apjab5063t2fna\"></a><sup> a</sup>yymmdd.\n<a name=\"apjab5063t2fnb\" id=\"apjab5063t2fnb\"></a><sup> b</sup>MJD-50000.\n<a name=\"apjab5063t2fnc\" id=\"apjab5063t2fnc\"></a><sup> c</sup>FWHM of the seeing disk in ''.\n<a name=\"apjab5063t2fnd\" id=\"apjab5063t2fnd\"></a><sup> d</sup>S/N for the PSF star within a circle of radius FWHM.\n<a name=\"apjab5063t2fne\" id=\"apjab5063t2fne\"></a><sup> e</sup><em>r</em>-SDSS magnitude.\n\n\n\n<p>Only a portion of this table is shown here to demonstrate its form and content. A <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"webref\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/suppdata/apjab5063t2_mrt.txt\">machine-readable</a> version of the full table is available.</p>\n\n\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-table-data\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/suppdata/apjab5063t2_mrt.txt\" target=\"_blank\">Data</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/suppdata/apjab5063t2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>To produce high-quality early light curves of PS J0147+4630, we selected the 70 observing epochs in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjab5063t2\">2</a> with FWHM\u00a0\u2264\u00a01<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />6, and removed two additional epochs in which the B magnitude deviates significantly from adjacent values (2018 August 16 and 28). In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f4\">4</a>, we display our final light curves of the quasar images (filled symbols). From the data at these 68 epochs, we also estimated typical magnitude errors. For each image, relying on theoretical grounds, we calculated the standard deviation between magnitudes having time separations \u22644.5 days (i.e., using 31 pairs of consecutive magnitudes), and then divided it by the square root of 2. The resulting errors are 0.0053 (A), 0.0058 (B), 0.0093 (C), and 0.0154 (D) mag. These typical errors were multiplied by the relative S/N at each epoch, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn5.gif\" alt=\"$\\left\\langle {\\rm{S}}/{\\rm{N}}\\right\\rangle /{({\\rm{S}}/{\\rm{N}})}_{\\mathrm{epoch}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\left\\langle {\\rm{S}}/{\\rm{N}}\\right\\rangle /{({\\rm{S}}/{\\rm{N}})}_{\\mathrm{epoch}}</script></span></span>, to obtain individual photometric uncertainties (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn6.gif\" alt=\"$\\left\\langle {\\rm{S}}/{\\rm{N}}\\right\\rangle $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\left\\langle {\\rm{S}}/{\\rm{N}}\\right\\rangle</script></span></span> is the average S/N; Howell <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib15\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib15\">2006</a>). We achieve ~0.5%\u20131.5% photometry over a period of about 1.6 yr, which includes an unavoidable visibility gap of more than 5 months. The effective sampling rate (excluding the long gap) is ~5 data per month.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjab5063f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjab5063f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0LT-IO:O <em>r</em>-band light curves of A, B, C, D, and the control star. The curves of B, C, D, and S (control star) are shifted by \u22120.2, \u22120.5, \u22122.0, and +1.0 mag, respectively, to facilitate comparison. The brightness records from all usable frames (see Table <a class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjab5063t2\">2</a>) are marked with filled and open symbols, while filled symbols trace the final light curves after removing 10 epochs (error bars of A, B, and C have sizes similar to those of symbols we use; see main text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjab5063f4\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadFigure/figure/apjab5063f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjab5063f4\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjab5063f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjab5063s3-2\" name=\"apjab5063s3-2\">3.2.\u00a0What Can We Learn from Early Light Curves of the Lensed Quasar?</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The expected time delays in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s2\">2</a> and the early light curves of ABCD in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s3-1\">3.1</a> are useful tools to analyze the origin and properties of the quasar variability in the <em>r</em> band. First, we obtained magnitude- and time-shifted light curves of image A as <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn7.gif\" alt=\"${m}_{\\mathrm{AY}}(t)={m}_{{\\rm{A}}}(t+{\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AY}})+\\left\\langle {m}_{{\\rm{Y}}}-{m}_{{\\rm{A}}}\\right\\rangle $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{m}_{\\mathrm{AY}}(t)={m}_{{\\rm{A}}}(t+{\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AY}})+\\left\\langle {m}_{{\\rm{Y}}}-{m}_{{\\rm{A}}}\\right\\rangle</script></span></span> for Y\u00a0= B, C, and D; and later, each <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn8.gif\" alt=\"$\\left[{m}_{\\mathrm{AY}}(t),{m}_{{\\rm{Y}}}(t)\\right]$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\left[{m}_{\\mathrm{AY}}(t),{m}_{{\\rm{Y}}}(t)\\right]</script></span></span> combined pair was stacked together. These three combined light curves are shown in the left panels of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f5\">5</a>. Second, we computed difference light curves in a standard way, i.e., <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn9.gif\" alt=\"${m}_{{\\rm{Y}}}(t)-{m}_{\\mathrm{AY}}(t)$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{m}_{{\\rm{Y}}}(t)-{m}_{\\mathrm{AY}}(t)</script></span></span> for Y\u00a0=\u00a0B, C, and D. For a given image Y, the dates in the magnitude- and time-shifted light curve of A, <em>m</em><sub>AY</sub>(<em>t</em>), were taken as reference epochs. Values of <em>m</em><sub>AY</sub>(<em>t</em>) were subtracted from averaged magnitudes of Y in bins with semiwidth <em>\u03b1</em> centered on the reference dates. We probed several reasonable values of <em>\u03b1</em>, obtaining difference curves consistent with each other, and then setting <em>\u03b1</em>\u00a0=\u00a05 days (see the right panels of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f5\">5</a>). The AB comparison (top panels) indicates that both images exhibit almost parallel variations, so the difference light curve has a noisy behavior around the zero level. Despite how extrinsic (microlensing) variability can be present, it should consist of short timescale fluctuations with amplitudes \u22640.02 mag. However, the situation is quite different from the other two AC (middle panels) and AD (bottom panels) comparisons. In both cases, we detect significant microlensing variations. The difference light curves for C and D include ~0.1 mag fluctuations over timescales from 100 to 400 days. Some other quads show similar levels of microlensing activity (e.g., Fian et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib11\">2018</a>; Gil-Merino et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib12\">2018</a>). We remark that microlensing signals in the D image rely on time delays \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AD</sub> predicted by Shajib et al.'s (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib27\">2019</a>) mass model and plausible values of <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>. Despite the true value of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn10.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AD}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AD}}</script></span></span> maybe being slightly out of the delay range used in this paper, this would not produce noticeable changes with respect to the similar signals in the bottom right panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f5\">5</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjab5063f5\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjab5063f5\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f5_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 5.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 5.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f5_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 5.</strong>\u00a0Combined and difference light curves in the <em>r</em> band. The original B, C, and D brightness records are compared with magnitude- and time-shifted light curves of A in the top, middle, and bottom panels, respectively. Left: combined curves. Right: difference curves. In the bottom right panel, in addition to the curve derived through the expected delay for <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> (filled symbols), we also show difference curves for two \"extreme\" values of <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> (e.g., Jackson <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib16\">2015</a>): 65 (solid line) and 75 (dotted line) km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. See main text for details.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjab5063f5\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadFigure/figure/apjab5063f5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjab5063f5\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjab5063f5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The LT-IO:O light curves of A and B over the two first monitoring seasons have similar shapes, providing evidence for intrinsic variability and enabling us to estimate <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn11.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AB}}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AB}}</script></span></span>. As we only try to show the potential of monitoring campaigns of PS J0147+4630, instead of an exhaustive analysis from several cross-correlation techniques, we exclusively used the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn12.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{4,2}^{2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{4,2}^{2}</script></span></span> dispersion estimator (Pelt et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib23\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib23\">1996</a>) to match both light curves. This method is simple and very popular, and it works in the presence of short timescale microlensing (e.g., Goicoechea &amp; Shalyapin <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib13\">2016</a>). A comprehensive study of all time delays will be done when much more extended light curves of the quad are available. First, in order to obtain \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AB</sub> and a constant magnitude offset \u0394<em>m</em><sub>AB</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0<em>m</em><sub>B</sub>(<em>t</em>)\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>m</em><sub>A</sub>(<em>t</em> + \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AB</sub>), we focused on a biparametric <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn13.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{4,2}^{2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{4,2}^{2}</script></span></span>. Second, we checked that reasonable values of the decorrelation length (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn14.gif\" alt=\"$\\delta \\,\\geqslant $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\delta \\,\\geqslant</script></span></span> 10 days) produce smooth dispersion spectra having minima at <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn15.gif\" alt=\"${\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AB}}\\lt $\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{\\rm{\\Delta }}{t}_{\\mathrm{AB}}\\lt</script></span></span> 0, and then chose <em>\u03b4</em>\u00a0=\u00a010 days. Third, we generated 3000 simulated light curves of each quasar image at epochs equal to those of observation. Each observed magnitude was modified by adding normally distributed random numbers with zero mean and standard deviation equal to the measured uncertainty. Fourth, the <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn16.gif\" alt=\"${D}_{4,2}^{2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{D}_{4,2}^{2}</script></span></span> estimator was applied to all (A, B) pairs of simulated curves. The distribution of magnitude offsets led to \u0394<em>m</em><sub>AB</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.248\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001 mag (1<em>\u03c3</em> confidence interval), and the time delay histogram is depicted in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f6\">6</a>. This yields an 1<em>\u03c3</em> interval \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AB</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22122.6<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn17.gif\" alt=\"${}_{-3.2}^{+1.1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{}_{-3.2}^{+1.1}</script></span></span> days, indicating that B is leading. Additionally, the median delay is in very good agreement with the expected value for <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> (vertical solid line in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f6\">6</a>; see the end of Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s2\">2</a>). Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f6\">6</a> also displays a vertical \"zipper\" indicating the narrow range of expected delays for <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a065\u221275 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjab5063f6\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjab5063f6\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f6_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 6.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 6.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f6_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 6.</strong>\u00a0Delay histogram from 3000 pairs of simulated curves AB. The best solutions of \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AB</sub> are derived from a <em>D</em><sup>2</sup><sub>4,2</sub> estimator (<em>\u03b4</em>\u00a0=\u00a010 days) with two free parameters: time delay and magnitude offset. Predicted time delays for <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a065\u221275 km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> are shown by a vertical \"zipper.\"</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjab5063f6\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadFigure/figure/apjab5063f6\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjab5063f6\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjab5063f6\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjab5063s4\" name=\"apjab5063s4\">4.\u00a0Summary</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Within the framework of the GLENDAMA project, we are analyzing archive data and conducting follow\u2013up observations of a sample of ten gravitationally lensed quasars (Gil-Merino et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib12\">2018</a>), and this paper focuses on the recently discovered Pan-STARRS quad PS J0147+4630 (Berghea et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib2\">2017</a>). After retrieving long-slit spectroscopic data in the Gemini Observatory Archive (Lee <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib19\">2018</a>), we use a robust multi-component fitting (e.g., Sluse et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib30\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib30\">2007</a>; Shalyapin &amp; Goicoechea <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib28\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib28\">2017</a>) to extract individual spectra of the main lensing galaxy and two quasar images in the observed crowded region. Despite both quasar spectra containing valuable imprints of intervening objects, we only study in detail the optical spectrum of G. This agrees very well with the spectral profile of an early-type galaxy at a redshift of 0.678, so the previous redshift determination through a heavily contaminated spectral energy distribution is very likely to be biased. An accurate estimate of <em>z</em><sub>G</sub> is crucial to predict time delays and carry out cosmological studies (e.g., Jackson <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib16\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib16\">2015</a>). We also measure a stellar velocity dispersion <em>\u03c3</em><sub>G</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0313\u00a0\u00b1\u00a014 km s<sup>\u22121</sup>, which is relevant, along with other results from ongoing observational efforts (e.g., macrolens flux ratios could be revealed by radio imaging with the Very Large Array; Berghea et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib2\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib2\">2017</a>), to better constrain the lensing mass distribution.</p><p>We have also conducted an early <em>r</em>-band monitoring of the four quasar images ABCD with the LT, and the corresponding light curves are used to probe the potential of optical monitoring campaigns. We take the new redshift <em>z</em><sub>G</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.678 to properly modify the time delays predicted by Shajib et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib27\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib27\">2019</a>), which permits us to construct reliable combined and difference light curves. These curves indicate that C and D images are affected by microlensing effects presumably produced by stars within G, and the microlensing-induced variations are promising tools to constrain the accretion disk size in PS J0147+4630 (e.g., Fian et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib11\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib11\">2018</a>; Morgan et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib22\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib22\">2018</a>). Lee (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib19\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib19\">2018</a>) also pointed out the presence of microlensing when comparing his single-epoch Gemini spectra of A and D. In addition, we find that A and B vary in an almost parallel way, suggesting that we basically detect intrinsic activity of the source quasar in both images. Using a single magnitude offset and a time delay to cross-correlate the light curves of A and B, we obtain \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AB</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0\u22122.6<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063ieqn18.gif\" alt=\"${}_{-3.2}^{+1.1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{}_{-3.2}^{+1.1}</script></span></span> days. Hence, as expected from lens modeling, A arrives a few days later than B. Although the \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AB</sub> estimation might be improved by considering two magnitude offsets or other sophisticated approaches, more extended brightness records are required to disentangle intrinsic from extrinsic (microlensing) signals in ABCD, and thus, to accurately measure the three independent delays \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AB</sub>, \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AC</sub>, and \u0394<em>t</em><sub>AD</sub>. These delays are essential pieces for a lens-based cosmology (e.g., Bonvin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib4\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib4\">2017</a>).</p></div> <div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We thank the anonymous referee for helpful comments and suggestions to improve the presentation of this paper. The Liverpool Telescope is operated on the island of La Palma by Liverpool John Moores University in the Spanish Observatorio del Roque de los Muchachos of the Instituto de Astrofisica de Canarias with financial support from the UK Science and Technology Facilities Council. This article is also based on observations obtained at the Gemini Observatory (acquired through the Gemini Observatory Archive and processed using the Gemini IRAF package), which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc., under a cooperative agreement with the NSF on behalf of the Gemini partnership: the National Science Foundation (United States), National Research Council (Canada), CONICYT (Chile), Ministerio de Ciencia, Tecnolog\u00eda e Innovaci\u00f3n Productiva (Argentina), Minist\u00e9rio da Ci\u00eancia, Tecnologia e Inova\u00e7\u00e3o (Brazil), and Korea Astronomy and Space Science Institute (Republic of Korea). We are also grateful to the MILES, Pan-STARRS, and SDSS collaborations for doing public databases. This research has been conducted in the framework of the Gravitational LENses and DArk MAtter (GLENDAMA) project, which is supported by the MINECO/AEI/FEDER-UE grant AYA2017-89815-P and the University of Cantabria.</p><p><em>Facilities:</em> Liverpool:2 m (IO:O) - , Gemini:Gillett (GMOS) - Gillett Gemini North Telescope.</p><p><em>Software:</em> IRAF (Tody <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib32\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib32\">1986</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib33\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib33\">1993</a>), pPXF (Cappellari &amp; Emsellem <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib6\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib6\">2004</a>; Cappellari <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib5\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib5\">2017</a>), IMFITFITS (McLeod et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib20\">1998</a>).</p></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjab5063app1\" name=\"apjab5063app1\">Appendix A: Extracting Individual Spectra of A, D, and G</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>To illustrate how the multi-component fitting works on instrumental flux distributions along the slit, we considered spatial flux distributions at wavelengths around 6800 \u00c5 for the first 1200 s spectroscopic exposure (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s2\">2</a>). By averaging over an 100 \u00c5 wavelength interval, we then obtained the spatial profile that appears in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f7\">7</a> (black filled circles). This 1D flux distribution was fitted to three skewed Moffat profiles with the same structure parameters (contributions of the three close sources A, D, and G; solid lines with different colors), resulting in a very good global solution (see A+D+G in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f7\">7</a>). We also show a fit to three Gaussian functions (dashed lines) for comparison purposes. These symmetric profiles do not reproduce the data in an accurate way, leading to significant fit residuals.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjab5063f7\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjab5063f7\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f7_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 7.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 7.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f7_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 7.</strong>\u00a01D flux distribution (along the slit) at ~6800 \u00c5. The black filled circles are the measured values, while the solid lines trace the global solution (black), and the individual contributions of A (red), D (blue), and G (green) using skewed Moffat profiles. Using Gaussian profiles, the global solution and the contribution of each source are also displayed as dashed lines.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjab5063f7\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadFigure/figure/apjab5063f7\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjab5063f7\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjab5063f7\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjab5063app2\" name=\"apjab5063app2\">Appendix B: Extracting Individual <em>r</em>-band Fluxes of A, B, C, and D</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>As an example of the photometric fitting procedure, we first selected the <em>r</em>-band frame on 2018 August 13 (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f3\">3</a>). The subframe of interest (containing the lens system) is shown in the left panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f8\">8</a>. Second, the 2D flux distribution in this subframe was modeled as four empirical PSFs (quasar images ABCD) plus a de Vaucouleurs profile convolved with the empirical PSF (main lensing galaxy G). The best-fit model from the IMFITFITS software package (McLeod et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib20\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib20\">1998</a>) has a reduced <em>\u03c7</em><sup>2</sup> of 1.28, which is a typical value when fitting system subframes at other epochs. The middle panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f8\">8</a> displays the residual signal after subtracting the four quasar images. Regarding this panel, it is worth noting that the fluxes of ABCD are one or two orders of magnitude larger than the flux of G, and the galaxy is an extended source. Additionally, residuals correspond to a relatively short exposure with a 2 m telescope. Hence, the light distribution in the middle panel is not dominated by emission from G. In the right panel of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjab5063f8\">8</a>, we also show the residual light after subtracting the full best-fit model (all sources). Pixels in this last subframe only contain the expected noisy signal.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjab5063f8\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjab5063f8\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f8_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 8.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 8.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/887/2/126/Full/apjab5063f8_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 8.</strong>\u00a0Left: 2D flux distribution in the <em>r</em>-band on 2018 August 13. Middle: residual fluxes after subtracting only the best-fit model for the quasar images. Right: residual fluxes after subtracting the full best-fit model. Residuals in the middle and right panels are linearly scaled between \u22123% and +3% of the maximum flux of A. The model consists of five components ABCDG and the fitting to data in the left panel is performed with IMFITFITS software (see main text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjab5063f8\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadFigure/figure/apjab5063f8\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjab5063f8\" href=\"/0004-637X/887/2/126/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjab5063f8\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>It is worthy to mention that we analyze a crowded system using a well-tested photometric method. This worked quite well in other gravitational lens systems, since light curves from the IMFITFITS method basically agreed with those from alternative techniques, even using different telescopes (Alcalde et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib1\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib1\">2002</a>; Ull\u00e1n et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib34\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib34\">2006</a>; Hainline et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib14\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib14\">2013</a>; Gil-Merino et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib12\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib12\">2018</a>). We also note that cross-talk between two close sources depends on seeing, and sometimes it produces evident deviations (with respect to adjacent magnitudes) in the light curves of both sources (e.g., see discussion on systematic effects and the corresponding outliers in Section 4 of Goicoechea &amp; Shalyapin <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjab5063bib13\" id=\"fnref-apjab5063bib13\">2016</a>). However, after removing data from frames with relatively poor seeing and two additional epochs producing evident outliers in the brightness record of the B image (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjab5063s3-1\">3.1</a>), our final light curves of PS J0147+4630 are not affected by significant systematic effects.</p></div></div><!-- End article full text -->\n<!-- Start Footnotes -->\n\t<h2 id=\"footnotes\">Footnotes</h2>\n\t\t<div data-mobile-collapse=\"\">\n\t\t\t<ul class=\"clear-list    <div class=\"partner-logo-alignment\">\n                <!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">Gravitational Lens System PS J0147+4630 (Andromeda's Parachute): Main Lensing Galaxy and Optical Variability of the Quasar Images</h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Luis J. Karazin Kharkiv National University, Svobody Sq. 4, 61022 Kharkiv, Ukraine</p></div><!-- End Affiliations --><!-- Start ORCIDs --><div class=\"wd-jnl-art-author-orcid-list\"><div class=\"replica-h4\">ORCID iDs</div><p class=\"mb-05\"><span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Luis J. Goicoechea</span><a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://orcid.org/0000-0003-0110-834X\" title=\"https://orcid.org/0000-0003-0110-834X\"><svg xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg\" viewBox=\"0 0 256 256\" width=\"20\" class=\"orcid-logo\"><path class=\"st0\" d=\"M256 128c0 70.7-57.3 128-128 128C57.3 256 0 198.7 0 128 0 57.3 57.3 0 128 0 198.7
